The brightest candidate, called A1703-zD1, has an observed (lensed) magnitude of 24.0 AB (26\u03c3) in the WFC3/IR F160W band, making it 0.2 mag brighter than the z <SUB>850</SUB>-dropout candidate recently reported behind the Bullet Cluster and 0.7 mag brighter than the previously brightest known z ~ 7.6 galaxy, A1689-zD1. With a cluster magnification of ~9, this source has an intrinsic magnitude of H <SUB>160</SUB> = 26.4 AB, a strong z <SUB>850</SUB> - J <SUB>125</SUB> break of 1.7 mag, and a photometric redshift of z ~ 6.7. Additionally, we find six other bright LBG candidates with H <SUB>160</SUB>-band magnitudes of 24.9-26.4, photometric redshifts z ~ 6.4 - 8.8, and magnifications \u03bc ~ 3-40. Stellar population fits to the Advanced Camera for Surveys, WFC3/IR, and Spitzer/Infrared Array Camera data for A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4 yield stellar masses (0.7 - 3.0) \u00d7 10<SUP>9</SUP> M <SUB>\u2609</SUB>, stellar ages 5-180 Myr, and star formation rates ~7.8 M <SUB>\u2609</SUB> yr<SUP>-1</SUP>, and low reddening with A<SUB>V</SUB> &lt;= 0.7. The source-plane reconstruction of the exceptionally bright candidate A1703-zD1 exhibits an extended structure, spanning ~4 kpc in the z ~ 6.7 source plane, and shows three resolved star-forming knots of radius r ~ 0.4 kpc. <P />Based on observations made with the NASA/ESA Hubble Space Telescope, obtained at the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy under NASA contract NAS5-26555. <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The American Astronomical Society (AAS), established in 1899 and based in Washington, DC, is the major organization of professional astronomers in North America. Its membership of about 7,000 individuals also includes physicists, mathematicians, geologists, engineers, and others whose research and educational interests lie within the broad spectrum of subjects comprising contemporary astronomy. The mission of the AAS is to enhance and share humanity's scientific understanding of the universe.</p> <p><a href=\"https://aas.org/\">https://aas.org/</a></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<!-- Partner logo tile starts -->\n<a href=\"\" class=\"overlay-launch\">\n    <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n</a>\n<span class=\"overlay-set\">\n    <div class=\"tint-screen\"></div>\n    <div class=\"overlay-panel\">\n        <a title=\"Close\"  class=\"close-icon close-overlay\" tabindex=\"0\" role=\"button\" aria-describedby=\"close-icon-description\"><span class=\"icon-close\"></span></a>\n        <p id=\"close-icon-description\" class=\"offscreen-hidden\">Click here to close this overlay, or press the \"Escape\" key on your keyboard.</p>\n        <div class=\"overlay-img\">\n            <a href=\"\">\n                <img border=\"0\" src=\"https://cms.iopscience.org/7ebd1b32-0439-11e9-b401-cfe9679c40e3/iop-2016.png?guest=true\" alt=\"The Institute of Physics, find out more\">\n            </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class=\"overlay-text\">\n            <p>The Institute of Physics (IOP) is a leading scientific society promoting physics and bringing physicists together for the benefit of all. It has a worldwide membership of around 50 000 comprising physicists from all sectors, as well as those with an interest in physics. It works to advance physics research, application and education; and engages with policy makers and the public to develop awareness and understanding of physics. Its publishing company, IOP Publishing, is a world leader in professional scientific communications.</p> <p><a href=\"https://www.iop.org\">https://www.iop.org</a></p></div>\n        <p class=\"ta-c mt-1 mb-2\"><a href=\"\"></a></p>\n    </div>\n</span>\n<!-- Partner logo tile ends -->\n\n<p></p>\n                </div>\n        </div>\n    </div>\n<!-- Branded journal header ends -->\n</div> <!-- end secondary-header -->\n<!-- Secondary header ends --><div class=\"da1-da2\" itemscope=\"\" itemtype=\"http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle\" id=\"page-content\">\n            <div class=\"da1 ta1 article-head\">\n                <!-- Start Eyebrow block, containing Surtitle and Labels -->\n<div class=\"eyebrow\">\n\t<!-- Start Collection Labels -->\n    <!-- End Collection Labels --> </div>\n<!-- End Eyebrow block -->\n\n<h1 itemprop=\"headline\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-title\">THROUGH THE LOOKING GLASS: BRIGHT, HIGHLY MAGNIFIED GALAXY CANDIDATES AT <I>z</I> ~ 7 BEHIND A1703<SUP>*</SUP>       </h1>\n\n<p class=\"mb-0\">\n\t<span data-authors=\"\">\n\t\t<span itemtype=\"http://schema.org/Person\" itemprop=\"author\" class=\"nowrap\"><span itemprop=\"name\">L. individual</a><a <span class=\"icon-newtab\">\n            </a></p>\n        </div>\n\n    <!-- End Email Alert -->\n<!-- End Email Alert --><!-- Start Citation Alert Link -->\n                        <p>\n<div class=\"jnl-notifications-wrapper\">\n    <a class=\"wd-jnl-email-alert\" href=\"https://myiopscience.iop.org/signin?origin=a0&return=https%3A%2F%2Fiopscience.iop.org%2Fmyiopscience%2Falerts%2Fsubscribe%3FarticleID%3D0004-637X%2F747%2F1%2F3\"><span\n            class=\"icon-alarm icon-alarm--jhp\"></span>Create citation alert</a>\n</div><!-- End Citation Alert Link -->\n                    </div>\n\t\t</div>\n    </div>\n    <!-- Article information ends -->\n<!-- Start Info top-->\n    <!-- end Info top --><div class=\"article-content\">\n\t<span id=\"articleId\" class=\"hide\">0004-637X/747/1/3</span>\n<!-- Start Abstract -->\n    <h2 id=\"artAbst\" class=\"collapse-blocked\">Abstract</h2>\n        <!-- Start article video abstract -->\n\t<!-- End article video abstract -->\n\t<div class=\"article-text wd-jnl-art-abstract cf\" itemprop=\"description\">\n                      <P>We report the discovery of seven strongly lensed Lyman-break galaxy (LBG) candidates at <I>z</I> ~ 7 detected in <I>Hubble Space Telescope</I> Wide Field Camera 3 (WFC3) imaging of A1703. The brightest candidate, called A1703-zD1, has an observed (lensed) magnitude of 24.0\u00a0AB (26\u03c3) in the WFC3/IR F160W band, making it 0.2\u00a0mag brighter than the <I>z</I>             <SUB>850</SUB>-dropout candidate recently reported behind the Bullet Cluster and 0.7\u00a0mag brighter than the previously brightest known <I>z</I> ~ 7.6 galaxy, A1689-zD1. With a cluster magnification of ~9, this source has an intrinsic magnitude of <I>H</I>             <SUB>160</SUB> = 26.4\u00a0AB, a strong <I>z</I>             <SUB>850</SUB> \u2013 <I>J</I>             <SUB>125</SUB> break of 1.7\u00a0mag, and a photometric redshift of <I>z</I> ~ 6.7. Additionally, we find six other bright LBG candidates with <I>H</I>             <SUB>160</SUB>-band magnitudes of 24.9-26.4, photometric redshifts <I>z</I> ~ 6.4 \u2013 8.8, and magnifications \u03bc ~ 3-40. Stellar population fits to the Advanced Camera for Surveys, WFC3/IR, and <I>Spitzer</I>/Infrared Array Camera data for A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4 yield stellar masses (0.7 \u2013 3.0) <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<SUP>9</SUP> <I>M</I>             <SUB>\u2609</SUB>, stellar ages 5-180\u00a0Myr, and star formation rates ~7.8 <I>M</I>             <SUB>\u2609</SUB>\u00a0yr<SUP>\u20131</SUP>, and low reddening with <I>A<SUB>V</SUB>             </I> &#x2264; 0.7. The source-plane reconstruction of the exceptionally bright candidate A1703-zD1 exhibits an extended structure, spanning ~4\u00a0kpc in the <I>z</I> ~ 6.7 source plane, and shows three resolved star-forming knots of radius <I>r</I> ~ 0.4\u00a0kpc.</P>       </div>\n    <!-- End abstract -->\n<!-- Start Export citation and abstract tools -->\n\t<p>\n\t\t<small>Export citation and abstract</small>\n\t\t<span class=\"btn-multi-block\">\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/747/1/3&doi=10.1088/0004-637X/747/1/3&exportFormat=iopexport_bib&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-bib\" title=\"Export BibTex\">BibTeX</a>\n\t\t\t<a href=\"/export?articleId=0004-637X/747/1/3&doi=10.1088/0004-637X/747/1/3&exportFormat=iopexport_ris&exportType=abs&navsubmit=Export+abstract\" class=\"btn btn-primary wd-btn-cit-abs-ris\" title=\"Export RIS\">RIS</a>\n\t\t</span>\n\t</p>\n<!-- End Export citation and abstract tools -->\n<!-- Start AAS Related Links -->\n<div class=\"reveal-container reveal-closed reveal-plus-icon bdt-1 mt-2 mb-2 wd-jnl-art-article-aas-related-links\">\n  <div class=\"replica-h3 mt-0\">\n    <a href=\"#\" class=\"reveal-trigger\" data-reveal-label-alt=\"Hide related links\">Related links</a>\n  </div>\n  <div class=\"reveal-content\">\n    <div class=\"article-meta\"> \n      <ul>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2012ApJ...747....3B\" target=\"_blank\">NASA ADS Record <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://nedwww.ipac.caltech.edu/cgi-bin/nph-objsearch?refcode=2012ApJ...747....3B&search_type=Search \" target=\"_blank\">NED Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"http://simbad.u-strasbg.fr/simbad/sim-ref?querymethod=bib&simbo=on&bibcode=2012ApJ...747....3B\" target=\"_blank\">Simbad Objects <span class=\"icon-newtab\"></span></a></li>\n      \t<li><a href=\"/journal/0004-637X/page/About%20Related%20Links\" target=\"_blank\">About Related Links</a></li>\n      \t</ul>\n    </div>\n  </div>\n</div>\n<!-- Start info bottom -->\n    <!-- End info bottom -->\n<!-- Start article full text -->\n\t<div xmlns:book=\"http://api.iop.org/Book/1.0/\" itemprop=\"articleBody\" class=\"wd-jnl-art-full-text article-text\">\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s1\" name=\"apj417478s1\">1.\u00a0INTRODUCTION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>The recently installed Wide-Field Camera 3 (WFC3) aboard the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) has led to a significant increase in the sample of <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxy candidates in the past year (Oesch et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r42\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r42\">2010b</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r9\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r9\">2010a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>; Bunker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r13\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r13\">2010</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r38\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r38\">2010</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r19\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r19\">2010</a>; Trenti et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r52\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r52\">2011</a>; Yan et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r54\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r54\">2011</a>). Already, more than 132 <em>z</em> ~ 7\u20138 Lyman-break galaxy (LBG) candidates (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>, see also Lorenzoni et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r35\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r35\">2010</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r39\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r39\">2011</a>) have been found in ultra-deep WFC3/IR observations of the Hubble Ultra-Deep Field (HUDF) and nearby fields, with even a few candidates at <em>z</em> ~ 8.5 and one at <em>z</em> ~ 10 (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r7\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r7\">2011a</a>). These observations provide our first glimpse of galaxies during the reionization epoch, showing a rapidly evolving galaxy luminosity function (LF) and a declining star formation rate with increasing redshift (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r7\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r7\">2011a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>). Recent studies of these <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxies have also looked at their structure and morphologies (Oesch et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r41\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r41\">2010a</a>), rest-frame <em>UV</em>-continuum slopes (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r10\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r10\">2010b</a>; Finkelstein et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r19\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r19\">2010</a>), and star formation rates and stellar masses (Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r32\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r32\">2010a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r33\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r33\">2010b</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r39\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r39\">2011</a>).</p><p>The ultra-deep observations are complemented by shallower wide-field WFC3/IR surveys for <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxies such as the Brightest of Reionizing Galaxies (Trenti et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r52\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r52\">2011</a>) and Hubble Infrared Pure Parallel Imaging Extragalactic Survey (Yan et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r54\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r54\">2011</a>), which so far have uncovered four bright (25.5\u201326.7) <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7.5 galaxies over 130 arcmin<sup>2</sup>. Over the next three years, the Cluster Lensing And Supernova survey with Hubble (CLASH; Postman et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r45\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r45\">2011</a>) and Cosmic Assembly Near-infrared Deep Extragalactic Legacy Survey (Grogin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r24\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r24\">2011</a>; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r29\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r29\">2011</a>) Multi-Cycle Treasury (MCT) programs will further augment the sample of bright <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxy candidates and our understanding of the high-redshift universe. These wide-field surveys are needed to characterize the bright end of the galaxy LF, where bright <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxies are rare. Placing tighter constraints of the number density of bright sources also helps break the degeneracy between the characteristic luminosity <em>L</em><sub>*</sub> and the faint-end slope \u03b1, a parameter whose value is crucial in determining the contribution of galaxies to the reionization of the universe.</p><p>The use of massive galaxy clusters as \"cosmic\" gravitational telescopes has uncovered some the brightest (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 26.5) <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 5 high-redshift galaxies to date (Franx et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r21\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r21\">1997</a>; Frye et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r22\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r22\">2002</a>; Kneib et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>; Egami et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r18\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r18\">2005</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>; Zheng et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r6\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r6\">2009</a>; Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) and some of the most distant galaxies known at the time of their discovery (Franx et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r21\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r21\">1997</a>; Kneib et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>). Gravitational lensing by massive galaxy clusters can amplify both the size and flux of background sources considerably. The increased spatial resolution allows high-redshift galaxies to be studied in unprecedented detail, providing clear views of their sizes and morphologies (e.g., Franx et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r21\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r21\">1997</a>; Kneib et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>; Zheng et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>; Swinbank et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r51\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r51\">2009</a>). This was clearly demonstrated with a very high source-plane resolution of 50 pc recently achieved by Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r56\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r56\">2011</a>) for the <em>z</em> = 4.92 galaxy behind MS1358. Likewise, the increased brightness can place <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxies within reach of ground-based spectroscopic follow-up observations.</p><p>Luminous high-redshift galaxies are extremely valuable because their spectra can provide direct measurements of the early star formation rate via Ly\u03b1 and H\u03b1 emission (Iye et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r26\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r26\">2006</a>) and the evolution of metallicity via metal emission and absorption lines (Dow-Hygelund et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r17\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r17\">2005</a>). The spectra of <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 objects also pinpoint the epoch of the intergalactic medium (IGM) reionization through the effect of neutral hydrogen in inhibiting the emission of Ly\u03b1 from galaxies (Santos <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r48\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r48\">2004</a>; Malhotra &amp; Rhoads <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r37\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r37\">2004</a>; Stark et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r50\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r50\">2010</a>). A truly neutral IGM will produce a damped Ly\u03b1 absorption profile (Miralda-Escude &amp; Rees <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r40\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r40\">1998</a>) that can be measured even at a low spectral resolution.</p><p>Here we present the discovery of seven bright strongly lensed LBG candidates at <em>z</em> ~ 7 behind the massive galaxy cluster A1703. The brightest candidate, A1703-zD1, is observed at 24.0\u00a0AB in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band, making it 0.2\u00a0mag brighter than the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate recently reported behind the Bullet Cluster (Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) and 0.7\u00a0mag brighter than the previously brightest known <em>z</em> ~ 7.6 galaxy A1689-zD1, found behind the massive cluster A1689 (Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>). This paper is organized as follows. We present the observations and photometry in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s2\">2</a> and dropout selection in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s3\">3</a>. In Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s4\">4</a> we discuss the source magnifications. We present the photometric redshifts in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s5\">5</a> and stellar population synthesis models in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s6\">6</a>. The results and the properties of the sources are discussed in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s7\">7</a>. We summarize our results in Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s8\">8</a>. Throughout this work, we assume a cosmology with \u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub> = 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.7, and <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> = 70\u00a0km\u00a0s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u00a0Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. This provides an angular scale of 5.2\u00a0kpc (proper) arcsec<sup>\u22121</sup> at <em>z</em> = 7.0. All magnitudes are expressed in the\u00a0AB photometric system (Oke <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r43\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r43\">1974</a>).</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s2\" name=\"apj417478s2\">2.\u00a0OBSERVATIONS AND PHOTOMETRY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apj417478s2-1\" name=\"apj417478s2-1\">2.1.\u00a0<em>HST</em> ACS and WFC3/IR Data</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We observed A1703 (<em>z</em> = 0.284; Allen et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r1\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r1\">1992</a>) with a single field of the Advanced Camera for Surveys (ACS) WFC in 2004 November as part of an ACS GTO program to study five massive galaxy clusters (HST-GO10325). The observations cover a 3<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />4\u2009<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u20093<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcm.gif\" alt=\"farcm\" align=\"baseline\" />4 field of view and consist of 20 orbits divided among six broadband filters: F435W (<em>B</em><sub>435</sub>; 7050\u00a0s), F475W (<em>g</em><sub>475</sub>; 5564\u00a0s), F555W (<em>V</em><sub>555</sub>; 5564), F625W (<em>r</em><sub>625</sub>; 9834\u00a0s), F775W (<em>i</em><sub>775</sub>; 11128\u00a0s), and F850LP (<em>z</em><sub>850</sub>; 17800\u00a0s). The ACS/WFC data were reduced with our ACS GTO APSIS pipeline (Blakeslee et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r5\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r5\">2003</a>). The reductions reach 5\u03c3 limiting magnitudes (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />19 diameter aperture) of 28.5, 28.6, 28.2, 28.6, 28.4, and 28.0 in the <em>B</em><sub>435</sub>, <em>g</em><sub>475</sub>, <em>V</em><sub>555</sub>, <em>r</em><sub>625</sub>, <em>i</em><sub>775</sub>, and <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> bands, respectively.</p><p>We obtained WFC3/IR observations of A1703 in the F125W (<em>J</em><sub>125</sub>) and F160W (<em>H</em><sub>160</sub>) bands, each with an exposure time of 2812\u00a0s, in 2010 April with the primary goal to search for <em>z</em> ~ 7 galaxies (HST-GO11802). The WFC3/IR observations cover the central 123''\u2009<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u2009136'' high-magnification region of the cluster (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>). The depths of the WFC3/IR data reach 5\u03c3 limiting magnitudes of 27.3 and 26.9 in a 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />45 diameter aperture for the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> bands, respectively.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f1\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f1\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f1_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 1.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 1.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f1_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 1.</strong>\u00a0Color image (<em>z</em><sub>850</sub><em>J</em><sub>125</sub><em>H</em><sub>160</sub>) of the galaxy cluster A1703 (<em>z</em> = 0.28). The locations of the high-redshift <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate galaxies are marked by red circles and ellipses. The image field of view is 123''\u2009<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u2009136'' and is shown with a position angle = 152\u00b0. The white contours represent the critical curves at <em>z</em> ~ 7. The dashed cyan and green ellipses denote the regions where the strong lensing model of Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) predicts counterimages for A1703-zD2 and A1703-zD5a/5b, respectively.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f1\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f1\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>For the reduction of both the ACS and WFC3/IR data, we weight each individual exposure by its inverse variance created from the sky background, modulated by the flat-field variations, along with the read noise and dark current. The drizzle combination procedure uses these inverse-variance images as weights and produces a final inverse-variance image for the combined, drizzled image in each filter. These inverse-variance weight images are used by SExtractor (Bertin &amp; Arnouts <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r4\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r4\">1996</a>) for both source detection and photometry (see Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s2-3\">2.3</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apj417478s2-2\" name=\"apj417478s2-2\">2.2.\u00a0<em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC Data</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We utilized archival <em>Spitzer</em>/Infrared Array Camera (IRAC) imaging of A1703 (program 40311) obtained over three epochs between 2007 December and 2008 June. We used the <em>Spitzer</em> MOPEX calibration pipeline to combine the data in the 3.6 and 4.5\u2009\u03bcm bands over the three epochs. The total exposure times were 18.9\u00a0ks in the 3.6 and 4.5\u2009\u03bcm bands, reaching 5\u03c3 limiting magnitudes of 24.7 and 24.1, respectively.</p></div><h3 id=\"apj417478s2-3\" name=\"apj417478s2-3\">2.3.\u00a0Photometry</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>We used SExtractor in dual-image mode for object detection and photometry. The detection image consisted of an inverse-variance weighted combination of the WFC3/IR <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> images. We smoothed the ACS optical images to match the WFC3/IR images and measured colors in small scalable Kron apertures (Kron factor of 1.2; Kron <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r30\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r30\">1980</a>). We then correct the fluxes measured in these smaller apertures to total magnitudes by using the flux measured in a larger Kron aperture (factor of 2.5) on the detection image. Likewise, we apply aperture corrections for light falling outside of the large Kron aperture using the tabulated encircled energies provided in the instrument handbooks.</p><p>We were able to obtain <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC fluxes for only two of the brighter and isolated sources. IRAC fluxes for these candidates were obtained using the deblending algorithm of Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r31\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r31\">2006</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r33\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r33\">2010b</a>). Briefly, this method involved using the higher resolution <em>HST</em> WFC3/IR images to create model IRAC images for the source and its nearby neighbors (assuming no differences between the structure or size of sources at 1.25 microns and IRAC wavelengths). We then vary the normalization of each model image, for both the source and its nearby neighbors, to fit the IRAC observations. Finally, we subtract the best-fit model profiles for the neighbors and perform photometry for the sources of interest in a 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5-diameter aperture. The IRAC errors include a component due to the modeling error. The modeling error can be quite large for sources near the edges of the WFC3/IR image because there is no source template for IRAC sources found beyond the WFC3/IR field of view.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s3\" name=\"apj417478s3\">3.\u00a0SELECTION OF <em>z</em> ~ 7 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-BAND DROPOUT CANDIDATES</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We search for <em>z</em> ~ 7 galaxies using a <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout selection criterion in two colours, based on the magnitudes measured in the small scalable apertures. We require candidates to have <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>\u2009&#x2265; 0.7 and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>\u2009&lt; 0.5. In addition, they must be undetected (&lt;2\u03c3) in each optical ACS band, with not more than one band showing a &gt;1.5\u03c3 detection. Further, candidates must be detected at &gt;5\u03c3 in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band. In cases where an object is not detected in a particular band, we assign the object with the 1\u03c3 detection limit to calculate object colors.</p><p>Because our <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> color criterion is slightly bluer than the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> &gt; 0.9 used by Bouwens et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>), we effectively extend our redshift selection window to somewhat lower redshifts. The use of the Bouwens et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>) color criterion, which was explicitly chosen to exclude source with redshifts <em>z</em> &lt; 6.5, would eliminate only one of our candidates.</p><p>Using these colour criteria, we identified seven <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout galaxy candidates with observed <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>-band magnitudes between 24.0\u2009and\u200926.4. The candidates are named in decreasing order of their brightness in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band, with the exception of the close pair of A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b. As discussed in the next section, A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b most likely represent two star-forming knots within a single source. We note that the A1703-zD5a component is detected in the <em>V</em><sub>555</sub> band at low significance (2.1\u03c3), but not in the overlapping <em>g</em><sub>475</sub> and <em>r</em><sub>625</sub> bands. Thus, we interpret the slight <em>V</em><sub>555</sub>-band detection as a likely statistical fluctuation.</p><p>All of the candidates are clearly resolved with the exceptions of our two faintest two candidates, A1703-zD6 and A1703-zD7. A1703-zD6 is unresolved with SExtractor stellarity parameter of 0.97. A1703-zD7 is somewhat extended, but only slightly resolved with a stellarity parameter of 0.5. Because A1703-zD6 is unresolved, under normal circumstances it cannot be ruled out as a low-mass L,T dwarf star. However, this candidate has subsequently been confirmed to be at <em>z</em> = 7.045 with deep Keck spectroscopic observations (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>).</p><p>While the WFC3/IR data were taken after the ACS optical data, we can rule we rule out supernovae as contaminants to our sample because the sources are either resolved or in the case of the unresolved source A1703-zD6, spectroscopically confirmed at <em>z</em> = 7.045.</p><p>The positions of these sources in the A1703 data are shown in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>. Their properties are listed in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a> and cutout stamps showing each of the sources are presented in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f2\">2</a>. The <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> colors of the candidates are illustrated in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f3\">3</a>. As seen in this figure, the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> color of A1703-zD2 is exactly at our selection limit (0.7). While it could be in our <em>z</em> ~ 7<em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout sample as a result of photometric scatter, this candidate is completely undetected in the deep optical ACS data. Its somewhat bluer <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> color means it is at the lower-redshift edge of our <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout selection window. This is completely consistent with its photometric redshift of <em>z</em> = 6.4 (see Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s5\">5</a>), making it our lowest redshift candidate.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f2\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f2\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f2_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 2.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 2.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f2_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 2.</strong>\u00a0Postage stamp cutout images of the high-redshift <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate galaxies from the <em>HST</em> ACS and WFC3/IR data. The cutout images are 6''\u2009<b>&#x00d7;</b>\u20096'', corresponding to 31.4\u00a0kpc on a side at <em>z</em> = 7, and are shown with a position angle = 130\u00b0. As discussed in the text, A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b most likely represent two star-forming knots within a single source.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f2\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f2\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f3\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f3\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f3_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 3.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 3.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f3_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 3.</strong>\u00a0<em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> vs. <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> two-color diagram used to select the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-band dropout candidates. The error bars and lower limits are 1\u03c3. The gray region represents the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> and <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> \u2212 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> colors of the selection criteria. The blue, green, and red lines show the expected colors of star-forming galaxies with UV-continuum slopes of \u03b2 = \u22121, \u22122, and \u22123 (<em>f</em><sub>\u03bb</sub>\u221d\u03bb<sup>\u03b2</sup>), respectively. The cyan, magenta, and yellow lines depict the expected colors of low-redshift interloper galaxies. The green region indicates the colors of low-mass L,T dwarf stars (e.g., Knapp et\u00a0al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r27\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r27\">2004</a>). While there is considerable overlap in the colors of L,T stars, only one of the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates (A1703-zD6) is unresolved. However, this candidate has been subsequently spectroscopically confirmed at <em>z</em> = 7.045 (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" confusion from neighboring sources or do not show an especially prominent (&gt;2\u03c3) detection.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn1\" id=\"apj417478t1fn1\"></a><sup> a</sup>The magnification errors represent the extreme values obtained from the minimum and maximum magnifications obtained within \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 of each candidate and assuming \u0394<em>z</em> \u00b1 1.0 for the source redshifts.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn2\" id=\"apj417478t1fn2\"></a><sup> b</sup>Photometric redshifts determined from the BPZ code (Ben\u00edtez <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r2\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r2\">2000</a>). Because of the limited depth of the optical data, there is a small chance that some of the sources could be at low redshift (see Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s5\">5</a>).\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn3\" id=\"apj417478t1fn3\"></a><sup> c</sup>As discussed in the text, A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b most likely represent two star-forming knots within a single source. The magnification of the combined A1703-zD5 source is 31.9<sup>+20.3</sup><sub>\u221210.6</sub>.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn4\" id=\"apj417478t1fn4\"></a><sup> d</sup>This component of the zD5 candidate is detected in the <em>V</em><sub>555</sub> band at low significance (2.1\u03c3), but not in the overlapping <em>g</em><sub>475</sub> and <em>r</em><sub>625</sub> bands. Thus, the slight <em>V</em><sub>555</sub>-band detection is likely a statistical fluctuation.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn5\" id=\"apj417478t1fn5\"></a><sup> e</sup>This candidate is spectroscopically confirmed to be at <em>z</em> = 7.045 (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>).\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-637X/747/1/3\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The best candidate, A1703-zD1, is an extremely bright <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate, with a <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitude of 24.0, that appears to be resolved in three separate knots (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f2\">2</a> and Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s7-2\">7.2</a>). In Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f4\">4</a> we present a histogram of both the observed and intrinsic (unlensed) <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes compared with the 73 <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates found in the HUDF09 and its two parallel fields and the WFC3/IR Early Release Science observations (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Histogram of the observed and intrinsic (unlensed) <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes for the seven <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout (<em>z</em> ~ 7) candidate galaxies identified behind A1703 (green and red) compared with the 73 <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates found in the HUDF09 and its two parallel fields and the WFC3/IR Early Release Science observations (blue; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s4\" name=\"apj417478s4\">4.\u00a0SOURCE MAGNIFICATIONS AND COUNTERIMAGES</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Several detailed studies to model the lensing of A1703 have been performed in recent years (Limousin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r34\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r34\">2008</a>; Richard et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r46\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r46\">2009</a>; Zitrin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>). We adopt the Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) A1703 strong lensing model to estimate the magnifications of the seven <em>z</em> ~ 7 sources and to identify possible counterimages. Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) used 16 multiply imaged systems behind A1703 and applied two independent strong lensing techniques to the high-quality, multiband ACS data, yielding similar results. Their strong lensing model places tight constraints on the inner mass profile, and thus provides reliable magnification estimates for background sources. The magnifications of the high-redshift candidates range from \u03bc ~ 3 to large magnifications of ~25\u201340, found for three of our sources that are located near the critical curve, where the magnification formally diverges. The magnification of each candidate is presented in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a>.</p><p>We estimated the magnification uncertainties by taking models extracted from the 1\u03c3 confidence level, as determined by the \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization of model, and marginalizing over the true 1\u03c3 errors. To make the error estimates more conservative, we also incorporate the range of magnifications obtained within \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 of each candidate and apply a \u0394<em>z</em> \u00b1 1.0 to the redshift of each source. Thus, the \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 shift is a measure of the magnification variance around the location of the source and the application of \u0394<em>z</em> \u00b1 1.0 accounts for the possible local uncertainty in the location of the critical curves. For objects that are close to the critical lines, the magnification errors are diverging due to their proximity to the critical curve, while objects far away will have a well-determined magnification as the latter slowly varies in regions away from the critical curve.</p><p>The brightest candidate, A1703-zD1, has a magnification of ~9, giving it an intrinsic magnitude of ~26.4 in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. The A1703 strong lensing model predicts counterimages for the three high-magnification candidates, A1703-zD2 and the pair of A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b, which are located nearby or on the high-redshift critical curve (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>). The lensing model predicts three counterimages for A1703-zD2 (\u03bc = 24.8; see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>). Taking into account the much smaller magnifications (\u03bc = 5.5\u20139.0) of the counterimages, they are predicted to have <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes between 26.0\u2009and\u200926.5. This is sufficiently bright that there was some possibility that we might locate them, but also a good chance we might not because they could easily be lost in the wings of a foreground galaxy. Despite an extensive search, we did not find any viable <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates near the predicted positions of the counterimages.</p><p>The close pair of A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b are also located in very close proximity of the critical curve and as such have high magnifications of \u03bc ~ 27\u201340. These candidates are also predicted to have counterimages on the other side of the brightest cluster galaxy (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>) with magnifications of \u03bc = 5.5, about five times less than A1703-zD5b. The predicted counterimages are expected to have an <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitude of &#x2265;27.0, which is fainter than our 5\u03c3 limiting magnitude of 26.9. Hence, it is not surprising that no <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates are found in the predicted region of the counterimages.</p><p>The critical curve lies only 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />6 from passing between the A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b sources, which is within the model (and redshift) uncertainty. To test the hypothesis that these two candidates are multiple images of the same source, we constructed a new model assuming that zD5a and zD5b are the same object. The resulting model is physically plausible and the predicted counterimage of this system, located in the same region marked in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>, is again fainter than the 5\u03c3 limiting magnitude of 26.9. Because the overall reproduction of all other systems remains the same, we cannot exclude this option based solely on the mass model. This possibility could also be supported by their similar colors, morphologies, and photometric redshifts.</p><p>However, because surface brightness is conserved in lensing, zD5a and zD5b should have the same surface brightness if they are indeed the same source. For zD5a and zD5b, we find surface brightnesses of 25.9 and 25.8 mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>, respectively, in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band and 26.4 and 25.9\u00a0mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>, respectively, in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. We note that these results are consistent with Oesch et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r41\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r41\">2010a</a>) who found a mean <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>band observed surface brightness of ~26\u00a0mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup> for a sample of <em>z</em> ~ 7 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-band dropouts candidates spanning 26 to 29\u00a0mag in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band. While their surface brightness agrees in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band, zD5b has a brighter surface brightness in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. On these grounds we conclude that zD5a and zD5b are two unique sources. Further, their very close proximity of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />76 in the image plane, with a magnification of 8.6 along the line separating them, translates to only ~480 pc in the source plane. Thus, even though we do not observe a diffuse component, which could have very low surface brightness below our detection limits, between them, we conclude that zD5a and zD5b are most likely two star-forming knots within a single source. The magnification of the combined A1703-zD5 source is 31.9<sup>+20.3</sup><sub>\u221210.6</sub>. We refer to the these sources separately because they appear as distinct sources in our catalog. The small elliptical Kron apertures used to measure their colors are well separated with sizes of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />34 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />26 and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />28 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />22, respectively.</p><p>We also considered the possibility that zD5a/b and zD2 were all counterimages of the same source. With zD5a/b representing two bright star-forming knots in a single candidate galaxy and not counterimages of the same source, we conclude that zD2 cannot be a counterimage of the zD5a/b source based simply on morphology. This was verified by constructing an additional model considering the center of zD2 and the center of zD5a/b as counter positions of the same source.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s5\" name=\"apj417478s5\">5.\u00a0PHOTOMETRIC REDSHIFTS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>To estimate the redshifts of the candidates, we used the Bayesian photometric redshift (BPZ) code (Ben\u00edtez <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r2\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r2\">2000</a>; Ben\u00edtez et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r3\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r3\">2004</a>; Coe et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r16\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r16\">2006</a>). Briefly, the photometric redshifts are based on a \u03c7<sup>2</sup>-fitting procedure to template spectra. Because the shape of the redshift distribution is not well calibrated at <em>z</em> ~ 7, we assumed a flat prior for all redshifts. The photometric redshifts of the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates are presented in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a> and their posterior <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>) probability distributions are shown in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f5\">5</a>. We find redshifts in the range of <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.4\u20138.8, with a median redshift of 6.7.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f5_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f5_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0Probability distributions of the photometric redshifts for each of the candidates. The vertical yellow line represents the redshift of the A1703 cluster (<em>z</em> = 0.28). As discussed in the text, A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b most likely represent two star-forming knots within a single source. The A1703-zD5a component shows the highest probability of being at low redshift due to its modest 2.1\u03c3 detection in the F555W band, which we attribute to a statistical fluctuation as described in the text.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The posterior probability distributions show that there is a small chance that A1703-zD3, A1703-zD5a, and A1703-zD7 could be at low redshift. Because of the modest 2.1\u03c3 detection in the F555W band, the A1703-zD5a knot shows the highest probability of being at low redshift. While we cannot completely exclude the low-redshift solutions for these candidates, objects in this magnitude range (24.0\u201326.4) with colors similar to LBGs would be rare and are more likely to be at high redshift. The BPZ results indicate that the exceptionally bright candidate A1703-zD1 has a narrow probability distribution at <em>z</em> = 6.7 and has the highest probability of being at high redshift, not showing any evidence to suggest a low-redshift solution.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s6\" name=\"apj417478s6\">6.\u00a0STELLAR POPULATION MODELS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We performed fits to the multiband <em>HST</em> and <em>Spitzer</em> photometry of A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4 using the stellar population models of Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r12\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r12\">2003</a>). We adopted a Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) initial mass function (IMF) with mass cutoffs of 0.1 and 100\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub> and models with subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> = 0.004) metallicities. The effect of dust reddening is included in the models using the Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r14\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r14\">2000</a>) obscuration law. We use the Madau (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r36\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r36\">1995</a>) procedure to correct the models for Lyman-series line-blanketing and photoelectric absorption. The stellar population models are constrained such that the stellar age must be less than the age of the universe at the fit redshift (e.g., 0.75 Gyr at <em>z</em> = 7.0). We consider two star formation histories (SFHs): simple (single-burst) stellar population (SSP) models and constant star formation rate (CSFR) models.</p><p>The best-fit stellar population models for A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4, the two sources for which we were able to obtain IRAC photometry, are shown in Figures\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f6\">6</a> and\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f7\">7</a>, respectively and the parameters are given in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t2\">2</a>. For these sources we find reasonably good model fits to the observed broadband photometry. For A1703-zD1, we note that the spectral energy distribution (SED) models are unable to fit the low flux in the IRAC 4.5\u03bcm band, resulting in a somewhat higher \u03c7<sup>2</sup><sub>\u03bd</sub> = 1.3\u20132.4</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f6\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f6\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f6_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 6.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 6.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f6_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 6.</strong>\u00a0Best-fit stellar population models to the observed multiband photometry of A1703-zD1. The models assume a Salpeter (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) IMF with subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub>) metallicity. The 2\u03c3 upper limits are shown for the ACS optical non-detections, but the models were fit to the measured fluxes and errors. The stellar masses are intrinsic values, corrected for the cluster magnification. The larger \u03c7<sup>2</sup><sub>\u03bd</sub> values (1.3\u20132.4) for these models results from the poor fit to the IRAC 4.5 \u03bcm-band data.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f7\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f7\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f7_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 7.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden;
