The magnification of the combined A1703-zD5 source is 31.9<sup>+20.3</sup><sub>\u221210.6</sub>.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn4\" id=\"apj417478t1fn4\"></a><sup> d</sup>This component of the zD5 candidate is detected in the <em>V</em><sub>555</sub> band at low significance (2.1\u03c3), but not in the overlapping <em>g</em><sub>475</sub> and <em>r</em><sub>625</sub> bands. Thus, the slight <em>V</em><sub>555</sub>-band detection is likely a statistical fluctuation.\n<a name=\"apj417478t1fn5\" id=\"apj417478t1fn5\"></a><sup> e</sup>This candidate is spectroscopically confirmed to be at <em>z</em> = 7.045 (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>).\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t1_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-637X/747/1/3\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t1_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>The best candidate, A1703-zD1, is an extremely bright <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate, with a <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitude of 24.0, that appears to be resolved in three separate knots (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f2\">2</a> and Section\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"secref\" href=\"#apj417478s7-2\">7.2</a>). In Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f4\">4</a> we present a histogram of both the observed and intrinsic (unlensed) <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes compared with the 73 <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates found in the HUDF09 and its two parallel fields and the WFC3/IR Early Release Science observations (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>).</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f4\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f4\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f4_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 4.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 4.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f4_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 4.</strong>\u00a0Histogram of the observed and intrinsic (unlensed) <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes for the seven <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout (<em>z</em> ~ 7) candidate galaxies identified behind A1703 (green and red) compared with the 73 <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates found in the HUDF09 and its two parallel fields and the WFC3/IR Early Release Science observations (blue; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r8\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r8\">2011b</a>).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f4\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f4\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s4\" name=\"apj417478s4\">4.\u00a0SOURCE MAGNIFICATIONS AND COUNTERIMAGES</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>Several detailed studies to model the lensing of A1703 have been performed in recent years (Limousin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r34\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r34\">2008</a>; Richard et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r46\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r46\">2009</a>; Zitrin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>). We adopt the Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) A1703 strong lensing model to estimate the magnifications of the seven <em>z</em> ~ 7 sources and to identify possible counterimages. Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) used 16 multiply imaged systems behind A1703 and applied two independent strong lensing techniques to the high-quality, multiband ACS data, yielding similar results. Their strong lensing model places tight constraints on the inner mass profile, and thus provides reliable magnification estimates for background sources. The magnifications of the high-redshift candidates range from \u03bc ~ 3 to large magnifications of ~25\u201340, found for three of our sources that are located near the critical curve, where the magnification formally diverges. The magnification of each candidate is presented in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a>.</p><p>We estimated the magnification uncertainties by taking models extracted from the 1\u03c3 confidence level, as determined by the \u03c7<sup>2</sup> minimization of model, and marginalizing over the true 1\u03c3 errors. To make the error estimates more conservative, we also incorporate the range of magnifications obtained within \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 of each candidate and apply a \u0394<em>z</em> \u00b1 1.0 to the redshift of each source. Thus, the \u00b10<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />5 shift is a measure of the magnification variance around the location of the source and the application of \u0394<em>z</em> \u00b1 1.0 accounts for the possible local uncertainty in the location of the critical curves. For objects that are close to the critical lines, the magnification errors are diverging due to their proximity to the critical curve, while objects far away will have a well-determined magnification as the latter slowly varies in regions away from the critical curve.</p><p>The brightest candidate, A1703-zD1, has a magnification of ~9, giving it an intrinsic magnitude of ~26.4 in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. The A1703 strong lensing model predicts counterimages for the three high-magnification candidates, A1703-zD2 and the pair of A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b, which are located nearby or on the high-redshift critical curve (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>). The lensing model predicts three counterimages for A1703-zD2 (\u03bc = 24.8; see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>). Taking into account the much smaller magnifications (\u03bc = 5.5\u20139.0) of the counterimages, they are predicted to have <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitudes between 26.0\u2009and\u200926.5. This is sufficiently bright that there was some possibility that we might locate them, but also a good chance we might not because they could easily be lost in the wings of a foreground galaxy. Despite an extensive search, we did not find any viable <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidates near the predicted positions of the counterimages.</p><p>The close pair of A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b are also located in very close proximity of the critical curve and as such have high magnifications of \u03bc ~ 27\u201340. These candidates are also predicted to have counterimages on the other side of the brightest cluster galaxy (see Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>) with magnifications of \u03bc = 5.5, about five times less than A1703-zD5b. The predicted counterimages are expected to have an <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitude of &#x2265;27.0, which is fainter than our 5\u03c3 limiting magnitude of 26.9. Hence, it is not surprising that no <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates are found in the predicted region of the counterimages.</p><p>The critical curve lies only 2<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />6 from passing between the A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b sources, which is within the model (and redshift) uncertainty. To test the hypothesis that these two candidates are multiple images of the same source, we constructed a new model assuming that zD5a and zD5b are the same object. The resulting model is physically plausible and the predicted counterimage of this system, located in the same region marked in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f1\">1</a>, is again fainter than the 5\u03c3 limiting magnitude of 26.9. Because the overall reproduction of all other systems remains the same, we cannot exclude this option based solely on the mass model. This possibility could also be supported by their similar colors, morphologies, and photometric redshifts.</p><p>However, because surface brightness is conserved in lensing, zD5a and zD5b should have the same surface brightness if they are indeed the same source. For zD5a and zD5b, we find surface brightnesses of 25.9 and 25.8 mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>, respectively, in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band and 26.4 and 25.9\u00a0mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup>, respectively, in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. We note that these results are consistent with Oesch et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r41\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r41\">2010a</a>) who found a mean <em>J</em><sub>125</sub>band observed surface brightness of ~26\u00a0mag arcsec<sup>\u22122</sup> for a sample of <em>z</em> ~ 7 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-band dropouts candidates spanning 26 to 29\u00a0mag in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band. While their surface brightness agrees in the <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band, zD5b has a brighter surface brightness in the <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> band. On these grounds we conclude that zD5a and zD5b are two unique sources. Further, their very close proximity of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />76 in the image plane, with a magnification of 8.6 along the line separating them, translates to only ~480 pc in the source plane. Thus, even though we do not observe a diffuse component, which could have very low surface brightness below our detection limits, between them, we conclude that zD5a and zD5b are most likely two star-forming knots within a single source. The magnification of the combined A1703-zD5 source is 31.9<sup>+20.3</sup><sub>\u221210.6</sub>. We refer to the these sources separately because they appear as distinct sources in our catalog. The small elliptical Kron apertures used to measure their colors are well separated with sizes of 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />34 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />26 and 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />28 <b>&#x00d7;</b> 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />22, respectively.</p><p>We also considered the possibility that zD5a/b and zD2 were all counterimages of the same source. With zD5a/b representing two bright star-forming knots in a single candidate galaxy and not counterimages of the same source, we conclude that zD2 cannot be a counterimage of the zD5a/b source based simply on morphology. This was verified by constructing an additional model considering the center of zD2 and the center of zD5a/b as counter positions of the same source.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s5\" name=\"apj417478s5\">5.\u00a0PHOTOMETRIC REDSHIFTS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>To estimate the redshifts of the candidates, we used the Bayesian photometric redshift (BPZ) code (Ben\u00edtez <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r2\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r2\">2000</a>; Ben\u00edtez et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r3\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r3\">2004</a>; Coe et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r16\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r16\">2006</a>). Briefly, the photometric redshifts are based on a \u03c7<sup>2</sup>-fitting procedure to template spectra. Because the shape of the redshift distribution is not well calibrated at <em>z</em> ~ 7, we assumed a flat prior for all redshifts. The photometric redshifts of the <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates are presented in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a> and their posterior <em>P</em>(<em>z</em>) probability distributions are shown in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f5\">5</a>. We find redshifts in the range of <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.4\u20138.8, with a median redshift of 6.7.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f5\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f5\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f5_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 5.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 5.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f5_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 5.</strong>\u00a0Probability distributions of the photometric redshifts for each of the candidates. The vertical yellow line represents the redshift of the A1703 cluster (<em>z</em> = 0.28). As discussed in the text, A1703-zD5a and A1703-zD5b most likely represent two star-forming knots within a single source. The A1703-zD5a component shows the highest probability of being at low redshift due to its modest 2.1\u03c3 detection in the F555W band, which we attribute to a statistical fluctuation as described in the text.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f5\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f5\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>The posterior probability distributions show that there is a small chance that A1703-zD3, A1703-zD5a, and A1703-zD7 could be at low redshift. Because of the modest 2.1\u03c3 detection in the F555W band, the A1703-zD5a knot shows the highest probability of being at low redshift. While we cannot completely exclude the low-redshift solutions for these candidates, objects in this magnitude range (24.0\u201326.4) with colors similar to LBGs would be rare and are more likely to be at high redshift. The BPZ results indicate that the exceptionally bright candidate A1703-zD1 has a narrow probability distribution at <em>z</em> = 6.7 and has the highest probability of being at high redshift, not showing any evidence to suggest a low-redshift solution.</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s6\" name=\"apj417478s6\">6.\u00a0STELLAR POPULATION MODELS</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We performed fits to the multiband <em>HST</em> and <em>Spitzer</em> photometry of A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4 using the stellar population models of Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r12\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r12\">2003</a>). We adopted a Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) initial mass function (IMF) with mass cutoffs of 0.1 and 100\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub> and models with subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> = 0.004) metallicities. The effect of dust reddening is included in the models using the Calzetti et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r14\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r14\">2000</a>) obscuration law. We use the Madau (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r36\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r36\">1995</a>) procedure to correct the models for Lyman-series line-blanketing and photoelectric absorption. The stellar population models are constrained such that the stellar age must be less than the age of the universe at the fit redshift (e.g., 0.75 Gyr at <em>z</em> = 7.0). We consider two star formation histories (SFHs): simple (single-burst) stellar population (SSP) models and constant star formation rate (CSFR) models.</p><p>The best-fit stellar population models for A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4, the two sources for which we were able to obtain IRAC photometry, are shown in Figures\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f6\">6</a> and\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f7\">7</a>, respectively and the parameters are given in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t2\">2</a>. For these sources we find reasonably good model fits to the observed broadband photometry. For A1703-zD1, we note that the spectral energy distribution (SED) models are unable to fit the low flux in the IRAC 4.5\u03bcm band, resulting in a somewhat higher \u03c7<sup>2</sup><sub>\u03bd</sub> = 1.3\u20132.4</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f6\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f6\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f6_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 6.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 6.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f6_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 6.</strong>\u00a0Best-fit stellar population models to the observed multiband photometry of A1703-zD1. The models assume a Salpeter (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) IMF with subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub>) metallicity. The 2\u03c3 upper limits are shown for the ACS optical non-detections, but the models were fit to the measured fluxes and errors. The stellar masses are intrinsic values, corrected for the cluster magnification. The larger \u03c7<sup>2</sup><sub>\u03bd</sub> values (1.3\u20132.4) for these models results from the poor fit to the IRAC 4.5 \u03bcm-band data.</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f6\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f6\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f7\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f7\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f7_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 7.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 7.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f7_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 7.</strong>\u00a0Best-fit stellar population models to the observed multiband photometry of A1703-zD4. The models assume a Salpeter (<a class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) IMF with subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub>) metallicity. <td colspan=\"1\" rowspan=\"1\">0.8</td>\n</tr>\n</tbody></table><p><small>\n<strong>Notes.</strong> Models assume a Salpeter (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r47\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r47\">1955</a>) IMF with mass cutoffs of 0.1 and 100\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub> and subsolar (<em>Z</em> = 0.2\u2009<em>Z</em><sub>\u2609</sub> = 0.004) metallicities.\n<a name=\"apj417478t2fn1\" id=\"apj417478t2fn1\"></a><sup> a</sup>Star formation history: simple (single-burst) stellar population (SSP) or constant star formation rate (CSFR) models.\n<a name=\"apj417478t2fn2\" id=\"apj417478t2fn2\"></a><sup> b</sup>Photometric redshifts derived from the stellar population fitting. These redshifts are consistent with those presented in Table\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"tabref\" href=\"#apj417478t1\">1</a>.\n<a name=\"apj417478t2fn3\" id=\"apj417478t2fn3\"></a><sup> c</sup>Best-fit stellar mass, corrected by the magnification at the fitted <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> redshift.\n<a name=\"apj417478t2fn4\" id=\"apj417478t2fn4\"></a><sup> d</sup>SFR-weighted mean stellar age (cf. F\u00f6rster Schreiber et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r20\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r20\">2004</a>). For a CSFR model, the weighted age is simply half of the time elapsed since the start of star formation.\n</small></p><p class=\"franklin fs-16\">\n            Download table as:\u00a0\n            <span class=\"btn-multi-block\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-ascii\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t2_ascii.txt?doi=10.1088/0004-637X/747/1/3\" target=\"_blank\">ASCII</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary wd-jnl-art-btn-typeset typeset-table-img\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/suppdata/apj417478t2_lr.gif\" target=\"_blank\">Typeset image</a></span></p></div><p>We find intrinsic (unlensed) stellar masses for both candidates in the range (0.7\u20133.0) <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<sup>9</sup>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub> with star formation rates of 7.3\u2009\u00b1\u20090.3\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>\u00a0yr<sup>\u22121</sup>and 8.2\u2009\u00b1\u20091.2\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>\u00a0yr<sup>\u22121</sup>, broadly consistent with those found for <em>z</em> ~ 6\u20138 galaxy candidates (Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r32\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r32\">2010a</a>, <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r33\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r33\">2010b</a>; Gonzalez et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r23\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r23\">2011</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r39\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r39\">2011</a>). Because these two candidates are located near the edge of the WFC3/IR field, there are no source templates for IRAC sources found beyond the WFC3/IR field of view. This results in a large modeling error for the neighboring sources, which we include in the total IRAC error for these candidates. While our modeling procedure weights each photometric data point by its inverse variance, because of the relatively large IRAC errors for these sources it should be noted that there is a larger uncertainty in the resulting stellar masses and ages derived from the stellar population models.</p><p>While we assumed a Salpeter IMF, fitting models using a Chabrier (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r15\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r15\">2003</a>) IMF would yield lower masses and star formation rates by a factor ~1.5. For both candidates, we note that the CSFR models provide consistently older SFR-weighted mean stellar ages than those for the SSP models. We find CSFR models with weighted ages of 100\u2013180 Myr, values again similar to that recently reported for a sample of <em>z</em> ~ 7\u20138 candidates (Labb\u00e9 et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r33\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r33\">2010b</a>; McLure et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r39\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r39\">2011</a>).</p></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s7\" name=\"apj417478s7\">7.\u00a0DISCUSSION</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><h3 id=\"apj417478s7-1\" name=\"apj417478s7-1\">7.1.\u00a0A1703-zD1 Brightness</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>Some of the brightest (<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/lesssim.gif\" alt=\"lesssim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 26.5) <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 5 high-redshift galaxies to date (Franx et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r21\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r21\">1997</a>; Frye et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r22\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r22\">2002</a>; Kneib et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>; Egami et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r18\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r18\">2005</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>; Zheng et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>; Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r6\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r6\">2009</a>; Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) have been identified in searches behind strong lensing clusters. Several of the more notable examples include the bright <em>i</em><sub>775</sub>-dropout galaxy, A1703-iD1, found by Zheng et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>) behind A1703. This candidate has a NICMOS/NIC3 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>-band magnitude of 23.9 and is lensed by a factor \u03bc ~ 3.1. From the SED fitting of this source, we found a photometric redshift of <em>z</em> = 5.95 \u00b1 0.15, which is consistent with the Keck spectroscopic redshift of <em>z</em> = 5.827 measured by Richard et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r46\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r46\">2009</a>).</p><p>At somewhat higher redshift, Kneib et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>) identified an exceptionally bright candidate (NIC3 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>= 24.1) behind the galaxy cluster A2218. This triply imaged candidate, A2218-iD1, lies near the high-redshift critical curve and has a large magnification of \u03bc ~ 25. While this very bright candidate has a similar <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>-band magnitude as A1703-zD1 and has been suggested to be at <em>z</em> ~ 7, it has a <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>110</sub> color of just ~0.4\u00a0mag, which is more consistent with a redshift of <em>z</em> = 6.3 \u00b1 0.1. It therefore almost certainly has a lower redshift than the present candidate A1703-zD1 and A1689-zD1, which is the brightest <em>z</em> ~ 7.6 candidate known. A1689-zD1 was discovered by Bradley et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>) behind the massive galaxy cluster A1689. This source is magnified by a factor of \u03bc ~ 9.3 and has a NIC3 <em>H</em><sub>160</sub> magnitude of 24.7, which is 0.7\u00a0mag fainter than the exceptionally bright candidate <em>z</em> ~ 7 candidate A1703-zD1 presented here. Most recently, Hall et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) reported the discovery of a very bright <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate behind the Bullet Cluster. The lensing model of the Bullet Cluster suggests that this candidate is doubly imaged with observed <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>-band magnitudes of 24.2 and 25.0 and magnifications of 8.4 and 12, respectively. However, because this candidate is detected in the <em>i</em><sub>775</sub> band, there is a fair chance this object could be a low-redshift interloper (Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apj417478s7-2\" name=\"apj417478s7-2\">7.2.\u00a0A1703-zD1 Source-plane Reconstruction and Morphology</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The large magnification of A1703-zD1 allows us an opportunity to examine the morphology of this exceptionally bright <em>z</em> ~ 6.7 galaxy candidate at very high spatial resolution. With a magnification of \u03bc ~ 9, the strong lensing effect provides an increased spatial resolution by about a factor ~3 compared to an unlensed source. This permits us to resolve spatial structures that would otherwise be unobservable in high-redshift <em>z</em> ~ 7 galaxies.</p><p>We used the Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) A1703 cluster lensing model to reconstruct A1703-zD1 in the source plane at <em>z</em> ~ 6.7. The deprojected image of A1703-zD1 in the WFC3/IR <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band is shown in Figure\u00a0<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" href=\"#apj417478f8\">8</a>. The linear magnification along the shear direction is 4.88<sup>+0.11</sup><sub>\u22120.14</sub> and 1.84 \u00b1 0.01 in the direction perpendicular to the shear direction. This candidate appears to be comprised of three resolved star-forming knots, each with a radius <em>r</em> ~ 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />08 (0.4\u00a0kpc) in the source plane. Altogether, A1703-zD1 has an extended linear morphology that spans ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />74 (~4\u00a0kpc) in the source plane at <em>z</em> = 6.7. Of course the physical size and structure we infer for this candidate is somewhat dependent on the details of the gravitational lensing model.</p><figure xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" id=\"apj417478f8\" tabindex=\"-1\" role=\"group\" class=\"boxout boxout-bdr-grey keyboard-focus-only\" data-toolbar-type=\"figure\" data-toolbar-link=\"apj417478f8\" data-toolbar-img=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f8_lr.jpg\" data-toolbar-title=\"Figure 8.\"><figure><div class=\"panzoom-container\"><div class=\"panzoom-parent\" style=\"overflow: hidden; position: relative;\"><img class=\"panzoom\" alt=\"Figure 8.\" src=\"https://static.iopscience.com/2.44.0/img/lazy-loading-placeholder.gif\" data-src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/images/0004-637X/747/1/3/Full/apj417478f8_lr.jpg\" style=\"transform: matrix(1, 0, 0, 1, 0, 0); backface-visibility: hidden; transform-origin: 50% 50% 0px; cursor: move; transition: transform 200ms ease-in-out 0s;\"></img></div><div class=\"buttons zoom-tools\"><button class=\"zoom-in\"><span class=\"icon-zoomin\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom In\n\t\t\t\t</button><button class=\"zoom-out\"><span class=\"icon-zoomout\"></span>\n\t                 Zoom Out\n\t\t\t\t</button><span class=\"mobile-block\"><button class=\"reset\"><span class=\"icon-loop\"></span>\n\t                     Reset image size\n\t\t\t\t\t</button></span></div></div><figcaption><div class=\"article-text figure-caption\"><p><strong>Figure 8.</strong>\u00a0Source-plane reconstruction of A1703-zD1 in the WFC3/IR <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> band. The source has an extended morphology that spans ~0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />74 (~4\u00a0kpc) in the source plane at <em>z</em> = 6.7. A1703-zD1 is comprised of three separate resolved knots, each with radius <em>r</em> ~ 0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />08 (~0.4\u00a0kpc). Of course the physical size and structure we infer for this candidate is somewhat dependent on the details of the gravitational lensing model. The white ellipse denotes the WFC3/IR <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> point-spread function in the source plane (0<img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/farcs.gif\" alt=\"farcs\" align=\"bottom\" />16 FWHM in the image plane).</p></div><p class=\"mb-05 print-hide\">Download figure:</p><span class=\"btn-multi-block print-hide\"><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-std-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-std-img-apj417478f8\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadFigure/figure/apj417478f8\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> Standard image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a><a class=\"btn btn-primary fig-dwnld-hi-img\" id=\"wd-jnl-art-btn-hires-img-apj417478f8\" href=\"/0004-637X/747/1/3/downloadHRFigure/figure/apj417478f8\"><span class=\"icon-image\"></span> High-resolution image\n\t\t\t\t\t</a></span></figcaption></figure></figure><p>There are now several examples of <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 5 lensed galaxy candidates that have morphologies consisting of star-forming knots (Franx et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r21\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r21\">1997</a>; Kneib et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r28\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r28\">2004</a>; Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>; Zheng et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>; Swinbank et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r51\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r51\">2009</a>; Zitrin et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r56\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r56\">2011</a>). Interestingly, each of the bright lensed candidates discussed in the previous section are extended and show significant substructure. In particular, both A1703-iD1 and A1689-zD1 show a pair of resolved star-forming knots. Additionally the pair of <em>z</em> ~ 6.5 dropout candidates, CL0024-iD1 and CL0024-zD1, each seem to consist of two components. With a separation of only 2\u00a0kpc in the source plane and nearly identical redshifts and properties (Zheng et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r55\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r55\">2009</a>), it is possible that CL0024-iD1 and CL0024-zD1 are spatially associated or merging galaxies. Recently, Oesch et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r41\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r41\">2010a</a>) even found extended features with resolved double cores in two unlensed <em>z</em> ~ 7 galaxies identified in the WFC3/IR HUDF. The apparent frequency of high-redshift galaxies showing substructure and multiple components is perhaps not surprising, but it provides strong evidence that both clumpy star formation and merging are important aspects of galaxy buildup at these very early epochs in the universe. The existence of substantial substructure is also expected based on studies of low-redshift Lyman-break analog galaxies (Overzier et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r44\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r44\">2008</a>).</p></div><h3 id=\"apj417478s7-3\" name=\"apj417478s7-3\">7.3.\u00a0Number Counts of <em>z</em> ~ 7 Candidates</h3><div class=\"article-text\"><p>The discovery of seven <em>z</em> ~ 7 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidates in a single cluster field is quite remarkable, especially since four of our candidates (zD1, zD3, zD6, and zD7) lie in a small region near the edge of the WFC3/IR image. While this may be surprising and call into question the reliability of these candidates, our confidence is bolstered by the spectroscopic confirmation at <em>z</em> = 7.045 (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>) of A1703-zD6, the second-faintest candidate. We consider the extremely bright (<em>H</em><sub>160</sub> = 24.0) candidate A1703-zD1, with a strong <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> break of 1.7, to be a rather robust high-redshift candidate, but we acknowledge that A1703-zD7, the faintest and nearly unresolved candidate, is certainly less secure than the other candidates.</p><p>While the cluster magnification increases the effective depth of the observations, the source-plane area that is surveyed at high redshift decreases inversely proportional to the magnification factor. The A1703 WFC3/IR image field of view is 4.6 arcmin<sup>2</sup>, but we estimate that we are effectively surveying only ~0.9 arcmin<sup>2</sup> in the <em>z</em> ~ 7 source plane. Thus, we derive a simple estimate of the number density of <em>z</em> ~ 7 sources in A1703 of 7.8 arcmin<sup>\u22122</sup>. Typically, blank field surveys such as the HUDF09 and its two parallel fields (Bouwens et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r7\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r7\">2011a</a>; Oesch et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r42\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r42\">2010b</a>) find ~3.5\u20134.3 <em>z</em> ~ 7 sources per arcmin<sup>2</sup>. While our number density is larger than that found in typical blank fields, if we allow for the possibility that zD7 is a low-redshift interloper, we are left with six sources or 6.7 arcmin<sup>\u22122</sup>. However, we note that cosmic variance in the number counts of high-redshift sources is significant in these relatively small-area <em>HST</em> fields (Trenti &amp; Stiavelli <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r53\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r53\">2008</a>), especially the cluster fields with their significantly reduced area in the high-redshift source plane.</p><p>We can place the observations of A1703 in context with those obtained for a small, but growing, sample of strong lensing clusters with high-quality optical and NIR multiband data. While Hall et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) have reported the discovery of 10 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropouts behind the Bullet Cluster (Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>), most cluster lensing fields have produced at most 1\u20132 <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 candidates. This includes NICMOS and WFC3/IR imaging of A1689 and the recent 16-band imaging of A383 and MACS1149 obtained by the CLASH MCT program. The apparent large variations in the number of <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 candidates discovered behind lensing clusters suggests, not surprisingly, that <em>z</em> <img src=\"https://cdn.iopscience.com/icons/Entities/gsim.gif\" alt=\"gsim\" align=\"baseline\" /> 7 galaxies may be highly clustered. One may therefore need to survey a large number of clusters to overcome the substantial large-scale structure effects.</p></div></div>\n<h2 class=\"header-anchor\" id=\"apj417478s8\" name=\"apj417478s8\">8.\u00a0SUMMARY</h2><div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We report the discovery of a very bright, highly magnified LBG candidate (A1703-zD1) at <em>z</em> ~ 6.7 behind the massive galaxy cluster A1703. A1703-zD1 is 0.2 mag brighter than the recently discovered <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout candidate behind the Bullet Cluster (Hall et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r25\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r25\">2011</a>) and 0.7\u00a0mag brighter than the current brightest known <em>z</em> ~ 7.6 galaxy A1689-zD1, identified behind the massive galaxy cluster A1689 (Bradley et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r11\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r11\">2008</a>). We find a strong <em>z</em><sub>850</sub> \u2212 <em>J</em><sub>125</sub> break of at least 1.7\u00a0mag and best-fit photometric redshift of <em>z</em> = 6.7. Using the Zitrin et\u00a0al. (<a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r57\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r57\">2010</a>) cluster lensing model, we estimate a magnification of \u03bc = 9 at <em>z</em> ~ 6.7 at the position of A1703-zD1. The candidate is extended, spanning ~4\u00a0kpc in the reconstructed source plane, and is resolved into three resolved star-forming knots. The source-plane deprojection shows that the star formation is occurring in compact knots of size ~0.4\u00a0kpc.</p><p>Additionally, we find six other bright <em>z</em> ~ 7 <em>z</em><sub>850</sub>-dropout galaxy candidates behind A1703. One of these candidates, A1703-zD6, has been subsequently confirmed with Keck spectroscopy to be at <em>z</em> = 7.045 (Schenker et\u00a0al. <a xmlns:xlink=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink\" class=\"cite\" href=\"#apj417478r49\" id=\"fnref-apj417478r49\">2012</a>). The candidates are observed with <em>H</em><sub>160</sub>-band magnitudes of 24.9\u201326.4, with a wide range of magnifications from 3\u2009to\u200940. Their photometric redshifts are found to be in the range of <em>z</em><sub>phot</sub> = 6.4\u20138.8, with a median redshift of 6.7. Using stellar population models to fit the rest-frame UV and optical fluxes for A1703-zD1 and A1703-zD4, we derive best-fit values for stellar masses (0.7\u20133.0) <b>&#x00d7;</b> 10<sup>9</sup>\u2009<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>, stellar ages 5\u2013180 Myr, and star formation rates ~7.8\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>\u2609</sub>\u00a0yr<sup>\u22121</sup>.</p><p>A1703-zD1, with a photometric redshift of <em>z</em> ~ 6.7 is the brightest observed <em>z</em> ~ 7 galaxy candidate found to date. We are planning to observe A1703-zD1 with near-IR spectroscopy to confirm its redshift and study its spectrum. Bright high-redshift galaxies such as these are valuable targets for ground-based spectroscopy and are pathfinding objects for future facilities such as the <em>James Webb Space Telescope</em>.</p></div>\n<div class=\"article-text\" data-mobile-collapse=\"\"><p>We thank Ivo Labb\u00e9 and Valentino Gonz\u00e1lez for assistance with the <em>Spitzer</em>/IRAC photometry. We also thank the anonymous referee whose comments and suggestions significantly improved the quality and clarity of this work. ACS was developed under NASA contract NAS 5-32865, and this research has been supported by NASA grants NAG5-7697 and HST-GO10150.01-A and by an equipment grant from Sun Microsystems, Inc. The Space Telescope Science Institute is operated by AURA Inc., under NASA contract NAS5-26555. Archival data were obtained from observations made by the <em>Spitzer Space Telescope</em>, which is operated by the Jet Propulsion Laboratory, California Institute of Technology under NASA contract 1407.</p></div></div><!-- End article full text -->\n<!-- Start Footnotes -->\n\t<h2 id=\"footnotes\">Footnotes</h2>\n\t\t<div data-mobile-collapse=\"\">\n\t\t\t<ul class=\"clear-list wd-content-footnotes\">\n\t\t\t\t<li class=\"indices-list\"><div class=\"indices-id\" name=\"apj417478fn1\" id=\"apj417478fn1\">*\u00a0</div><div class=\"indices-content\"><p class=\"mb-0\"><p>Based on observations made with the NASA/ESA <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em>, obtained at the Space Telescope Science Institute, which is operated by the Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy under NASA contract NAS5-26555.
